=500  \\$aThe Instrumentation in Judith consists of two flutes, two french horns, two oboes, two bassoons, two violins, a viola, timpani, a harp, and basso continuo consisting of alternating harpsichord and organ. The harp is only called for in one movement, Wake my Harp! to melting measures sung by Abra in act 1.

=100  \\$aGrétry, André-Ernest-Modeste$d1741-1813$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q210962$94756
=245  \\$aSilvain.$bComédie en un acte et en vers
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bGrétry$aLyon$bCastaud$bSerrières$c1770
=300  \\$a[ii]-134 pages$bmanuscript pensil notes on frontmatter
=500  \\$aSilvain, a one-act opéra-comique, was one of Grétry's biggest early successes. The plot concerns Silvain, who works as a poor farmer after being disinherited by his rich father for marrying a lower-class woman. The pastoral theme and its celebration of rural life was common in opéra-comique of the time but Marmontel's libretto goes much further in advocating social equality and defending the rights of peasants against the encroachment of landowners. 
=500  \\$acontains spoken texts as well

=041  \\$aita
=100  1\$aTestori, Carlo Giovanni$d1714-1782$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3659433$94797
=245  \\$aLa musica ragionata :$bespressa famigliarmente in dodici passeggiate a dialogo
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aVercelli$bPanialis$c1767
=300  \\$a[viii]-cli-[1] pages$b22 folded sheets of music examples
=500  \\$aCarlo Giovanni Testori (1714-1782) was an Italian composer, violinist and music theorist. In his birthplace Vercelli, he was active as a music teacher and violin professor. He composed masses, motets and instrumental music but his fame is mainly linked to the treatise 'La musica ragionata', published in Vercelli by Giuseppe Panialis in 1767. In this and subsequent works (based on Rameau's theory), Testori summarises the treatises of the 17th and 18th centuries, expounding musical notions in the form of lively and witty dialogue.

=520  \\$aMarcus Tullius Cicero (106 BC-43 BC) was a Roman statesman, lawyer, scholar, philosopher, writer and Academic skeptic, who tried to uphold optimate principles during the political crises that led to the establishment of the Roman Empire. =041  \\$agrc$alat
=100  \\$aHomeros$d9th Century BC-8th Century BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6691$94802
=245  \\$aIlias
=260  \\$aOxford$bs.n.$c1665
=300  \\$a[xiii]-767-139-[1] pages$bengraved frontispiece & folded, illustrated sheet inserted
=500  \\$aThe Iliad ("a poem about Ilium (Troy)") is one of two major ancient Greek epic poems attributed to Homer. It is one of the oldest extant works of literature still widely read by modern audiences. As with the Odyssey, the poem is divided into 24 books and was written in dactylic hexameter. It contains 15,693 lines in its most widely accepted version. Set towards the end of the Trojan War, a ten-year siege of the city of Troy by a coalition of Mycenaean Greek states, the poem depicts significant events in the siege's final weeks. In particular, it depicts a fierce quarrel between King Agamemnon and a celebrated warrior, Achilles. It is a central part of the Epic Cycle. The Iliad is often regarded as the first substantial piece of European literature.

=500  \\$aHero and Leander is the Greek myth relating the story of Hero, a priestess of Aphrodite (Venus in Roman mythology) who dwelt in a tower in Sestos on the European side of the Hellespont, and Leander, a young man from Abydos on the opposite side of the strait. =500  \\$aCorrect year? The Neaulme edition began in 1747? Gayot de Pitaval (1673-1743) was a French lawyer who recorded numerous pithy scandals, such as de Affaire des Poisons
=500  \\$aA cause célèbre is an issue or incident arousing widespread controversy, outside campaigning, and heated public debate. The term continues in the media in all senses. It is sometimes used positively for celebrated legal cases for their precedent value and more often negatively for infamous ones, whether for scale, outrage, scandal, or conspiracy theories. The term is a French phrase in common usage in English. In French, cause means, here, a legal case, and célèbre means "famous". The phrase originated with the 37-volume Nouvelles Causes Célèbres, published in 1763, which was a collection of reports of well-known French court decisions from the 17th and 18th centuries.

=041  \\$afre
=245  \\$aHistoire du théâtre de l'Académie royale de musique en France depuis son établissement jusqu'à présent
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bDuchesne$c1757
=300  \\$a2 vols. (320+221-[7]-11 pages)
=500  \\$aHistory of the theatre of the Royal Academy of Music of France, from its establishment to the present. It traces the history of the Academy of Music from its foundation in 1669 to the ordinances which regulate its internal functioning. It contains information on the opera house balls, biographies of librettists and composers, a staff statement as of July 1756, and other valuable details. A double catalogue (chronological and alphabetical) of the operas represented between 1645 and 1752, a very detailed index and a bibliography of works devoted to opera make this book an essential tool for research on 18th-century opera.

=041  \\$afre$hgrc
=100  \\$aBoileau Despréaux, Nicolas$d1636-1711$4aut$4trl$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q188857$94839
=245  \\$aŒuvres diverses$bavec Le Traité du Sublime ou du merveilleux dans le discours$nvol. 2
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bSchelte$c1713
=300  \\$a344 pages$btitle page in red and black ink, 2 engraved frontispieces
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$asee also 06N04
=500  \\$aOn the Sublime is both a treatise on aesthetics and a work of literary criticism. It is written in an epistolary form and the final part, possibly dealing with public speaking, has been lost. The treatise is sometimes dedicated to Posthumius Terentianus, a cultured Roman and public figure, though little else is known of him. On the Sublime is a compendium of literary exemplars, with about fifty authors spanning 1,000 years mentioned or quoted. Along with the expected examples from Homer and other figures of Greek culture, Longinus refers to a passage from Genesis.

=500  \\$aSecond part is a fragment from "Pasquin, from death returned: Or His Journey, Done in the Other World: Presented in a dialogue between him and Marforio. Translated from the Italian, increased and improved. Accompanied by several fine Copperplates.editied by Christiaan Karstensz, Amsterdam, 1677.
The dialogue on death is held between two of the most famous statues of Roman antiquity: Pasquino, whose name always designated the satire, and Marforio, the best known statue, who was represented with the image of Neptune. There seems to exsist an English translation of this work entitled "Pasquin risen from the dead, or his own relation of a late voyage he made to the other world. London, 1674" .

=041  \\$alat
=245  \\$aSatyræ
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHack$c1648
=300  \\$a[xvi]-644-[42] pages$bbound in white vellum, title page engraving
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aSee also 03F16 and 05B03 for different Dutch editions
=500  \\$aJuvenal's Satires is a series of 16 satirical poems, divided between 5 books. The poems meditate on life in Rome under the Emperor Domitian, and his successors. The Satires are especially well known for their uniquely caustic style, which is often contrasted with the urbane and witty style of Juvenal’s predecessor, Horace.
=500  \\$aPersius strikes the highest note that Roman satire reached; in earnestness and moral purpose he rises far superior to the political rancour or good-natured persiflage of his predecessors and the rhetorical indignation of Juvenal. 
=500  \\$ainteresting title page engraving by Reinier van Persijn (1615-1668) : allegory of discord: Elevation on which a woman in two minds. In her hands is a burning heart, symbolising virtue, and a mask, representing vice. She is flanked by a personification of America and Avarice. In the background, two satyrs are holding the curtain open for a window. The personification of Truth is crowned by angels. Below the image, in a cartouche, is the title in Latin.

He then devoted himself to literature under the pseudonym (de) Boispréaux and in particular to translation, in association with Gottfried Sellius.

=500  \\$aCyrus II of Persia (c. 600–530 BC) commonly known as Cyrus the Great, was the founder of the Achaemenid Empire, the First Persian Empire. Under his rule the empire embraced all of the previous civilized states of the ancient Near East, expanded vastly and eventually conquered most of Western Asia and much of Central Asia. Spanning from the Mediterranean Sea and Hellespont in the west to the Indus River in the east, the empire created by Cyrus was the largest the world had yet seen.

=500  \\$aDiarium Europaeum (Latin for 'Journal of Europe') was a journal of history and current affairs founded by Martin Meyer, who wrote under the name Philemerus Irenicus Elisius. It was published between 1659 and 1683 in 45 volumes, and later renamed Allgemeine Schau-Bühne der Welt (German for 'Theatre of the World'). Wilhelm Serlin served as publisher from the journal's inception until Serlin's death. The journal focussed on contemporary events as opposed to chronicles of more distant times

Teutschen Reiche, bey allgemeiner Reichs-Versammlung zu Regenspurg, und Stillung der, in der Chur-Pfaltz und selbiger Nachbarschafft am Rhein-Strohm, wie auch in dem Hertzogthum Bremen, entstandener Kriegs-Unruh; So dann, ausser demselben, in anderen nah und fern gelegenen Königreichen und Republicken, absonderlich aber in Polen, wegen Niederdrückung der innerlichen Empörungen, deßgleichen zwischen Engelland und den vereinigten Niederlanden, wie auch zwischen diesen, den vereinigten Niederlanden, und dem Herrn Bischoff zu Münster, in Kriegs-Sachen, zu Wasser und Land, und sonst anderwärts, bey andern Begebenheiten, in der Welt hin und wieder, theils im 1665. und theils im 1666. Jahrs, publicirtes Laudum oder Compromißlichen Außspruch; Wie nicht weniger, zwischen der Cron Schweden und gemeiner Stadt Bremen, deroselben Vocation, Session und Votum, in dem Reichs-Städte-Rath, betreffend, vormahls und itzt, Und dann zwischen theils Chur- und Fürsten deß Reichs und andern außwärtigen Potentaten und Republicken, in Verträgen, Bündnüssen und Deductionen, in abgewichenem Jahretractiret und abgehandelt worden.

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aMarpurg, Friedrich Wilhelm$d1718-1795$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q548897$94794
=245  \\$aAbhandlung von der Fuge
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aBerlin$bHaude und Spener$c1753
=300  \\$a2 volumes in 1 ([iv]-xvi-192-[4]+[iv]-xxx-147-[14] pages) + 2 volumes of music examples (lx+lxii pages)
=500  \\$aThe first volume is divided into eight chapters and begins with a definition of three music-theoretical terms: Repetition of the same note values in the same voice; transposition of a sequence of notes by a certain interval; and imitation, i.e. processing a sequence of notes by means of repetition or transposition. Marpurg goes on to discuss the various possibilities of setting dux and comes, the fugue theme and its response, which are here called Führer and Gefährte.

In terms of content, the second volume deals with more complex forms of counterpoint. 

At numerous points in the treatise, excerpts from Bach's fugues are given as examples, especially from the Art of Fugue, the Musikalisches Opfer also comes up, as well as his two-part inventions.
=500  \\$avol. 1 has engravings on the title-page and at pages 30, 37, and 146

=100  \\$aShaw, James$4aut$94878
=245  \\$aSketches of the History of the Austrian Netherlands
=260  \\$aLondon$bRobinson$c1786
=300  \\$a310 pages
=500  \\$aThe Austrian Netherlands was the territory of the Burgundian Circle of the Holy Roman Empire between 1714 and 1797. The period began with the Austrian acquisition of the former Spanish Netherlands under the Treaty of Rastatt in 1714 and lasted until Revolutionary France annexed the territory during the aftermath of the Battle of Sprimont in 1794 and the Peace of Basel in 1795. Austria relinquished its claim on the province in 1797 by the Treaty of Campo Formio.

=500  \\$aJohann Christian Kittel's importance can be seen above all in the cultivation and transmission of Bach's tradition, his performance practice and his works, especially as he is also regarded as his "last pupil". In this context, he placed particular emphasis on the musical arrangement of church services and the role of organ playing. He applied his musical ambition above all to the elaboration of playable organ music. In this context, he also wrote this three-volume textbook on organ playing, which was one of the most outstanding works of its kind at the time

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aMusikalische Neujahrsgedichte
=260  \\$aZürich$bMusiksaal$c1761-77
=300  \\$a[126] pages$b17 illustrated plates inserted
=500  \\$aThe Musikgesellschaft ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ began to publish New Year's pieces in 1685; see 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, 26D03, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=520  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.

=100  \\$aVergilius$d70 BC-19 BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1398$94960
=245  \\$aDes Publius Virgilius Maro Werke$nvols. 1-3
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aBraunschweig$bVieweg$c1822
=300  \\$a3 volumes in 1 (295-320-342-[2] pages)
=500  \\$aPublius Vergilius Maro (70-19 BC), usually called Virgil or Vergil, was an ancient Roman poet of the Augustan period. He composed three of the most famous poems in Latin literature: the Eclogues (or Bucolics), the Georgics, and the epic Aeneid. A number of minor poems, collected in the Appendix Vergiliana, were attributed to him in ancient times, but modern scholars consider his authorship of these poems to be dubious.

=260  \\$aRome$bFei$c1662
=300  \\$a60 pages
=500  \\$aBonifazio Graziani's numerous motets for solo voice and for 2, 3, 4 voices, published in dozens of printed collections, and two oratories on a Latin text, Adae oratorium and Filii prodigi oratorium, are particularly memorable. He is considered, together with Giacomo Carissimi and Francesco Foggia, to be one of the most representative composers of Roman sacred music in the concertato style of the 17th century. A large part of his production was published posthumously, by his brother Graziano Graziani and his nephew Domenico Graziani, as ordered by the composer in his will.

=500  \\$aGaius Julius Phaedrus or Phaeder (c. 15 BC–c. 50 AD) was a 1st-century AD Roman fabulist and the first versifier of a collection of Aesop's fables into Latin. Nothing is recorded of his life except for what can be inferred from his poems, and there was little mention of his work during late antiquity. It was not until the discovery of a few imperfect manuscripts during and following the Renaissance that his importance emerged, both as an author and in the transmission of the fables.

=100  \\$aEeden, Frederik van$d1860-1932$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q211514$94949
=245  \\$aVan de passielooze lelie
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bVersluys$c1901
=300  \\$a159-[1] pages
=500  \\$aSee also 09E03
=520  \\$aIn the collection of poetry 'Van de passielooze lelie' (1901), Frederik van Eeden expressed his desire to merge with God through suffering and agony, as he makes himself known in music, nature and selfless love. Critics were divided over this collection: according to De Amsterdammer, Van Eeden was half apostle and half minister, but Den Gulden Winckel called him a great poet and an exalted mystic.

=100  \\$aEeden, Frederik van$d1860-1932$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q211514$94949
=245  \\$aDe broeders:$btragedie van het recht
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bVersluys$c1894
=300  \\$a253 pages
=500  \\$aThe 'Tragedie van het recht' is a play titled 'De Broeders' by Frederik Van Eeden, written in sixteen acts, without rhyme and in five-foot iambic verse. In the play, Van Eeden ponders whether God is just and what the meaning of suffering is. According to critics, 'De Broeders' has some similarities to Goethe's 'Faust' and Dante's 'Divina Commedia'.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe publishers Valerius Maximus and Junius Juvenalis in the 1st volume are false/made up. The 1st volume is a reprint (date unknown) from the original in 1715, containing poetry from diverse authors. The third volume is added by printer Hendrik Bosch - a decision probably caused by the success of the first two volumes - and was mainly written by Gysbert Tysens (1693-1732) (more information: https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/zijd002gysb01_01/zijd002gysb01_01_0001.php)
=500  \\$aThe edition of the 1st volume is probably also printed by H. Bosch; in the back matter is a section called 'catalogus van boeken by Gerrit Bouman', a printer who was working together with Bosch. 
=500  \\$aValerius Maximus (fl. 14-37) was the author of the historical anecdotes 'Factorum ac dictorum memorabilium libri IX', written during the reign of Tiberius

=500  \\$aMarcus Valerius Martialis was a Roman poet from Hispania (modern Spain) best known for his twelve books of Epigrams, published in Rome between AD 86 and 103, during the reigns of the emperors Domitian, Nerva and Trajan. In these short, witty poems he cheerfully satirises city life and the scandalous activities of his acquaintances, and romanticises his provincial upbringing. He wrote a total of 1,561 epigrams, of which 1,235 are in elegiac couplets. Martial has been called the greatest Latin epigrammatist and is considered the creator of the modern epigram. Along with Roman graffiti, the Epigrams are important sources for Latin obscene words.  
=500  \\$aNothing is known of this Vincentius Collesso, who claims to be a jurist and has no other publications to his name. Even his name is unstable: it is Vincentius Collesso at the head of the edition, Vincentius Colessus in the catalogue of the Ad usum Delphini collection found at the end of the preface to Ausone's edition (1730), Vincentius Collesius in the Bibliotheca Latina of J. A. Fabricius (t. 1, p. 465), Vincent Collés in the Nouvelle Biographie générale, t. 33, p. 1019, Vincent Collesson in the Catalogue général des livres imprimés de la BN, and finally Colesson in the British Museum Catalogue of printed Books. Given the poor philological quality of this work, there is no reason to regret that the name of its author has been forgotten.

=100  \\$aStoke, Melis$dc.1235-c.1305$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q380956$95053
=245  \\$aRijmkronijk$bmet Historie- Oudheid- en Taalkundige Aanmerkingen$n1-3/3
=260  \\$aLeiden$bMair, le$c1772
=300  \\$a[viii]-615 pages$bmarbled cardboard binding, linen corners, gilde embossed linen spine, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aMelis Stoke was a Dutch writer who lived in the 13th century. He started writing in 1290 in Middle Dutch a chronicle in rhyme on the countship of Holland. His most famous work was the Rijmkroniek, the chronicle in rhyme, among the first books written in the Dutch language. In it is the account of the murder of count Floris V. Stoke found his information from written sources, eyewitness accounts and his own observations. Among modern historians, however, he is not known for his historical reliability.
=500  \\$aRhyming chronicles are chronological descriptions of historical facts and persons set in rhyme. The genre of the vernacular rhyming chronicle originated in Holland and Flanders in the mid-13th century and remained in vogue until the second half of the 15th century.

=500  \\$aOne of multiple auctions held at Drouot in 1919
=500  \\$aThe 12 plates contain photographs of furniture and art works. The images are monochromatic but have a cream colored background, the images of the furniture have been manipulated (cut out from background, numbers added). One of the plates contains the subscript: 'Helio Léon Marotte Paris', which suggests these are heliographs.
=500  \\$aThis auction was held after the death of Léontine Estelle Denain (1844-1919), who had been married to composer Léo Delibes (1836-1891). Delibes had died in his fifties, his last years had been financially stable and socially secure. His spouse Léontine was the daughter of a well known actress. Apparently the couple (or Léontine alone?) had acquired a considerable art collection.

=500  \\$aThe Theatre was a magazine published in London between 1877 and 1897. It contained reviews of theatre productions around the world, theatrical news, short stories, verse and biographical sketches of important figures of the time, written by prominent critics, playwrights, managers and actors, and illustrated with Woodburytype photographs. Its longest-serving editor was Clement Scott, the most influential British drama critic of his time, and under his editorship The Theatre was regarded as the leading British theatre magazine.

=500  \\$aContains the appendix 'Buch von der Meister-Singer holdseligen Kunst, Anfang, Fortübung, Nutzbarkeiten, und Lehrsätzen', which is the first research into the Meistersinger tradition. It discusses the origin of the guild, their Tabulaturen and customs. It also includes music examples by Müglin, Heinrich Frauenlob, Der Marner and Barthel Regenbogen. Though its accuracy has been doubted since the time of its publication, it remains an important account and formed the basis of accounts by Jean Paul and E. T. A. Hoffmann, as well as Richard Wagner's opera Die Meistersinger von Nürnberg. [after wikipedia article on Johann Christoph Wagenseil]

=008  231010s1781\\\\|||a||||\||||\00|\p\dut\d
=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aBilderdijk, Willem$d1756-1831$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1375186$94900
=245  \\$aMijn verlustiging
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLeiden$bvan Hoogeveen$c1781
=500  \\$aWillem Bilderdijk (1756-1831) was a Dutch poet, historian, lawyer, and linguist.
=500  \\$aIt was not until 1781 that the definitive edition of Bilderdijk's first lyric collection appeared anonymously. It opened with a short introduction, defending the genre of erotic poetry 'against the timidity of heavy-handed moralists', on the grounds that even when 'the Minnedichten depict their own lust...', this is done only to 'make the sense of pleasure... (to) depend on the immaterial lust of souls ..., on that union of will, of heart, of soul, which is the essence of love'.

On closer inspection, this introduction appears to have been taken from one of the appendices to Bilderdijk's 'Verhandeling over het verband van dichtkunst en welsprekendheid met de wijsbegeerte' (1783), which was awarded a prize in 1780, and this alone largely negates the anonymity of the edition. This anonymity was in fact immediately compromised by the simultaneous publication by the same publisher of a 'Supplement', consisting of a fable signed with the letter B ('Vertelling voor de minnedichteren en hunne lezeren'), preceded by a poem of praise by François Halewijn on the collection 'Mijn Verlustiging', in which Bilderdijk is directly mentioned as the author.
(Translated by Deepl from https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/_spi007197801_01/_spi007197801_01_0009.php)

=500  \\$aHugo/Huig de Groot (1583-1645) was a Dutch humanist
=500  \\$aGrotius composed a poem titled "Bewijs van den waren godsdienst" in a prison cell in 1620 after having been arrested by Prince Mauris. This didactic poem, whose title translates as "Proof of the True Religion," was first published in 1622 as a defense of Christianity against other religions and atheism. The Latin version of this poem, De Veritate Religionis Christianae ("On the Truth of the Christian Religion"), was later published in 1627.” The work contains six "books" with the first three touting the merits of Christianity, and the last three attacking paganism, Judaism, and Islam, respectively

=500  \\$aPrinted by Laurent Biesse (1643-1713); specific date unknown
=500  \\$aThe 'Regola delli cinque ordini d'architettura' presented Vignola's practical system for constructing columns in the five classical orders (Tuscan, Doric, Ionic, Corinthian and Composite) utilising proportions which Vignola derived from his own measurements of classical Roman monuments. The clarity and ease of use of Vignola's treatise caused it to become in succeeding centuries the most published book in architectural history. (Source: Wikipedia)

=500  \\$aJacques Goudstikker (1897-1940) was a Jewish-Dutch art dealer whose collection was seized by the Germans during WWII
=500  \\$aThe Goudstikker art dealers were the largest, most influential and most specialised in the Netherlands. Goudstikker traded works by seventeenth-century Dutch painters such as Rembrandt, Willem van de Velde the Elder, Salomon van Ruysdael and Jan van der Heyden in a way that is no longer possible with such masterpieces, because they are only publicly auctioned as exceptions and have actually become museum pieces. Some other masterpieces: Claude Lorrain, Jan van Goyen, Jan Steen, Gerard ter Borch, Filippino Lippi and Jacopo del Casentino.

=500  \\$aThe Goudstikker art dealers were the largest, most influential and most specialised in the Netherlands. Goudstikker traded works by seventeenth-century Dutch painters such as Rembrandt, Willem van de Velde the Elder, Salomon van Ruysdael and Jan van der Heyden in a way that is no longer possible with such masterpieces, because they are only publicly auctioned as exceptions and have actually become museum pieces. =100  \\$aKalkbrenner, Friedrich$d1784-1849$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q170270$95135
=245  \\$aMéthode pour apprendre le piano-forté à l'aide du guide-mains
=250  \\$a5th ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bs.n.$c18xx
=300  \\$a77 pages
=500  \\$awith signature/stamp 'F. Kalkbrenner'
=500  \\$aWhile living 1814 to 1823 in England, Kalkbrenner came across an invention made by Johann Bernhard Logier. This invention was the so-called chiroplast or "hand guide" ("guide-main" in french, "Handleiter" in german). The chiroplast was a contrivance made from two parallel rails of mahogany wood that were placed on two feet and loosely attached to the piano. This apparatus should restrict vertical motions of the arms thereby helping nascent pianists to attain the (perceived) correct position of the hands. This invention became a runaway success. There are reports that it was still available for sale in London in the 1870s. In 1817, Logier teamed up with Kalkbrenner to found an academy where music theory and piano playing, of course with the help of the chiroplast, were taught. The proceeds from the patent made Kalkbrenner a wealthy man.

=100  \\$aBeauharnais, Hortense de$d1783-1837$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q229875$95142
=245  \\$aThe Knight Errant,$bWritten and Composed by the Queen of Holland
=260  \\$aNew York$bRiley$c18xx
=300  \\$a[2] pages
=500  \\$aLoose sheet containing a strophic song for voice and piano: "The Knight Errant" or originally "Partant pour la Syrie" (Departing for Syria) was composed by Hortense de Beauharnais; the text was written by Alexandre de Laborde in or about 1807. The song was inspired by Napoleon's Egypt campaign. It represents a chivalric composition of the aspirations of a crusader knight in a style typical for the First French Empire. Hortense indicated in her Memoires that she wrote the music when she lived at Malmaison. During its popularity in the nineteenth century the song was arranged for numerous instruments by various composers.
=500  \\$aThe poem by Labarde was originally titled "Le beau Dunois", telling the story of the handsome crusader Dunois. Prior to his departure to Syria he prays to the Virgin Mary that he will love the most beautiful woman and that he himself may be the bravest.
=500  \\$aHortense de Beauharnais (1783-1837) was the daughter of Joséphine de Beauharnais, who married Napoleon, and mother of Napoleon III. She was Queen of Holland due to her (short) marriage (1806-1810) with Napoleon's brother Louis Napoléon (1778-1846).

=245  \\$aTwo Sonatas for the Piano-forte or Harpsichord, with Accompaniments, For the Violin, German Flute & Violoncello$bOp.2
=260  \\$aLondon$bRiley$c1792
=300  \\$a4 parts (13 + 3 + 3 + 5 pages) 
=500  \\$aCecilia Maria Barthélémon (1767-1859) was a singer, composer, pianist and organist. Barthélemon was married twice. She inscribed her name into her copies of Haydn's music with two different names. On one copy, she had the name Cecilia Maria Hinchcliffe.
A second copy had the name Cecilia Maria Henslow. Barthélemon married Captain E.P. Henslow around December 1796. She stopped performing publicly at this time. 
=500  \\$amore on the composer: https://spot.colorado.edu/~hayesd/18c%20Women/cm-barthelemon.html
=500  \\$aComplete set of four parts, each with its own title-page
=500  \\$aComposer's Stamp CeMH (Cecilia Maria Hinchcliffe) on title page of the violin part
=500  \\$aDedicated to her Royal Highness the Dutchess of York, one of Haydn’s many English friends and patrons during his stay in London in the 1790ies.
=500  \\$aThe op. 2 sonatas were reprinted around 1803, the copy in the New York Public Library being the composer's autographed presentation copy to Henslowe. 
=500  \\$aSonata I: For the violin
Allegro Moderato  (con espresione) - Andante/Andantino.  A favourite Minuet from Dr. Arne's Lessons/The Favorite Minuet with Variations by Dr. Arne - Rondo presto
Sonata II: for the flute
Allegro Moderato - Rondo vivace

=100  \\$aMancini, Francesco$d1672-1737$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1356310$95152
=245  \\$aXII Solos for a Violin with a Thorough Bass
=246  \1$a xii. Solos for a Violin or Flute
=260  \\$aLondon$bWalsh$c17xx
=300  \\$a[ii]-55 pages
=500  \\$aThe first edition was published in London, probably in 1724, by John Barrett and William Smith. It differs in 2 details from this Walsh-edition: the title page: xii. Solos for a Violin "or Flute", and Geminiani's involvement was not mentioned. Besides that, the print of the music is a perfect copy.
Francesco Geminiani's name was probably added for purely commercial reasons by the publisher. Apparently Mancini's sonatas were well received, as another reprint appeared in 1727. 
Presumably in 1724 Walsh published a re-issue: here too, the plates are the same as above, only the title-page is different, and there is no dedication. 
=500  \\$aDedicated to John Fleetwood Esq, who was the English Consul General in Naples and had returned to England in 1722.
=590  \\$aDedicated to the Hon.ble John Fleetwood Esq. Consull Gen.ll for the Kingdom of Naples. Which Solos are Proper Lessons for the Harpsichord. carefully Revis'd and Corrected By Mr. Geminiani.

=245  \\$aSix English Cantatas after the Italian Manner
=260  \\$aLondon$bWalsh & Hare$c[1716]
=300  \\$a[vi]-28 pages
=500  \\$aEngraved title page
=500  \\$aSet of six solo continuo cantatas for alto/mezzo, each existing of 2 recitatives and 2 arias
=500  \\$aApart from an early Ann Arbor Facsimile reprint from the 1970ies, there seems to be no digital example available as yet
=505  \\$gI. "Venus! Thy Throne of Beauty" / text: Mr Hughes -- II. The Reconciliation / Texts: Mr Congreve -- III. Apollo and Daphne / Text: Mr Hughes -- IV. "Beneath a verdant Lawrels" / text: Mr Prior -- V. "While on your blooming Charms" / Text: Mr Hughes -- VI. "Young Strephon" / Text: Mr Hughes
=520  \\$aThe English cantata would retain a place on recitals and benefit concerts throughout the eighteenth century, performed in venues as diverse as the parlors private homes, the stages of opera houses, and the pleasure gardens of Vauxhall, of Ranelagh, and Marylebone. Composers such as Galliard, Henry Carey, John Stanley, Thomas Ame, William Boyce, Thomas Linley Jr., and James Hook would continue to compose English cantatas until the decline of the genre around 1790. (Jennifer Cable, Composing after the Italian Manner: The English Cantata 1700-1710, University of Richmond, 2014)

=100  \\$aKobrich, Johann Anton$d1714-1791$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q21995252$95158
=245  \\$aGründliche Klavierschule, durchgehends mit praktischen Beyspielen erkläret
=260  \\$aAugsburg$bRieger$c1782
=300  \\$a[ii]-47 pages
=500  \\$aJohann Anton Kobrich, the son of the organist of the 'Landsberger Stadtpfarrkirche' Maximilian Adam Kobrich († 1730), succeeded him at the age of 16 and filled this office until his death. After his wife died in 1782, he turned to theology and was ordained a priest. He wrote works for piano and organ, as well as masses, litanies and vespers. Several of his works were printed in Nuremberg and Augsburg and circulated widely in Central and Eastern Europe.

=100  \\$aGherardi, Evaristo$d1663-1700$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3592734$95163
=245  \\$aLe Théâtre Italien de Gherardi,$bou le Recueil General de toutes les Comedies & Scenes Françoises par les Comediens Italiens du Roy
=260  \\$aParis$bCusson$bWitte$c1700
=300  \\$a6 volumes ([xxx]-648-[10]+[iv]-552+[ii]-614-[8]+[iv]-592-[40]+[iv]-549-[22]+[ii]-682-[42] pages)$binserted plates, frontispiece engraving, music
=500  \\$aEvaristo Gherardi was the Harlequin of the Comédie-Italienne, which was abolished in 1697
=500  \\$aSee 08E02 for the Amsterdam 1701 ed. of the 'Théâtre italien'
=500  \\$aEach play is preceded by a beautiful engraved plate depicting a scene (55 in total)
=500  \\$aEach volume is concluded with the related songs (notated for voice and basso continuo)
=500  \\$aLiterature: W. John Kirkness, Le français du théatre italien d'après le receuil de Gherardi 1681-1697 (Geneva: Droz, 1971)
=505  \\$gvol. 1: Arlequin Mercure galant (1682) - La matrone d'Éphèse ou Arlequin Grapignan (1682) - La Lingère du palais (1682) - Arlequin Protée (1683) - Arlequin Empereur dans la lune (1684) - Arlequin Jason ou La Toison d'Or comique (1684) - Arlequin Chevalier du Soleil (1685) - Isabelle medecin (1685) - Colombine avocat pour et contre (1685) - Le Banqueroutier (1687) - La precaution inutile (1692) --$gvol. 2: La Cause des femmes - La Critique de la cause des femmes -- Le Divorce (1688) -- Le Marchand dupé (1688) -- La Femme vangée -- La Descente de Mezzetin aux Enfers -- Le Grand Sophy -- Arlequin homme à bonne fortune (1690) -- La Critique de l'homme à bonne fortune --$gvol. 3: Les Filles errantes (1690) - La Fille sçavante (1690) - La Coquette ou L'Académie des dames (1691) - Arlequin Ésope (1691) - Les Deux Arlequins (1691) - Le Phénix (1691) - Arlequin Phaeton (1692) - Ulisse et Circé (1691) -- $gvol. 4: L'Opéra de campagne (1692) - L'Union des deux opéras (1692) - La Fille de bon sens (1692) - Les Chinois (1692) - La Baguette de Vulcain (1693) - Les Adieux des officiers ou Vénus justifiée (1693) -- Les Mal-assortis (1693) - Les Originaux ou L'Italien (1693) - Les Avantures des Champs Élisées (1693) --$gvol. 5: Les Souhaits - La Naissance d'Amadis (1694) - Le Bel-esprit (1694) - Arlequin défenseur du beau sexe - La Fontaine de sapience (1694) - Le Départ des comédiens (1694) - La Fausse coquette (1694) - Le Tombeau de Maître André (1695) - Attendez-moy sous l'orme (1695) --$gvol. 6: La Thèse des dames (1695) - Les Promenades de Paris (1695) - Le Retour de la Foire de Bezons (1695) - La Foire Saint Germain (1695) - Les Momies d'Égypte (1696) - Les Bains de la Porte S. Bernard (1696) - Arlequin Misantrope (1696) - Pasquin et Marforio (1697) - Les Fées (1697)
=520  \\$aAll these plays of a comic and burlesque nature were performed from 1682 to 1697, mainly at the Hôtel de Bourgogne. There are many harlequinades, several plays by Regnard or adapted from the Italian theatre by Regnard, and plays by Le Noble. There is a great variety of subjects, mythological, oriental, and generally on everything that was in the air at the time, such as the play on the mummies of Egypt... This type of theatre, primarily intended for entertainment, was very popular at the end of the 17th century and had a lasting influence on French theatre.
=534  \\$aLe Théâtre italien, ou Recueil de toutes les scènes françoises qui ont esté jouées sur le théâtre italien de l'Hostel de Bourgogne$c1694
=590  \\$apendant tout le temps qu'ils ont été au Service. Enrichi d'Estampes en Taille-douce à la tête de chaque Comedie, à la fin de laquelle tous les Airs qu'on y a chantez se trouvent gravez notez, avec leur Basse continue chiffrée?
